Establishing 'Adala and the Hierarchy of Ta'dil and Jarh
Definition of 'adala with hierarchy of ta'dil and jarh terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shuhra and tazkiya as methods of establishing 'adala and classify the levels of ta'dil and jarh terms used by hadith scholars.

Core Idea
'Adala is established either by widespread fame (shuhra) or explicit commendation (tazkiya), with a hierarchy of terms for praise and criticism.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the reliability of narrators (riwayah) is fundamental. This passage provides the foundational taxonomy for evaluating 'adala (trustworthiness) through two key methods: shuhra (fame) and tazkiya (explicit commendation). It then details the standard hierarchical terms used by hadith scholars for both praise (ta'dil) and criticism (jarh), and concludes with a nuanced discussion on whether multiple weak chains can strengthen a narration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methods of establishing 'adala
Locate in the text the two means by which a narrator's 'adala is known: shuhra (fame) and tazkiya (explicit commendation). Note that shuhra is considered superior.
Shuhra is exemplified by the great imams who are so well-known that questioning their 'adala is unnecessary.
2
Understand the superiority of shuhra over tazkiya
Read the examples of Ahmad ibn Hanbal and Yahya ibn Ma'in objecting to inquiries about famous scholars. This illustrates that shuhra renders tazkiya redundant.
3
Memorize the hierarchy of ta'dil terms
List the terms from highest to lowest: hujja, thiqah, hafiz, dabit (highest); then ma'mun, sadaq, la ba's bihi; then salih, shaykh, hasan al-hadith, suwaylih.
The highest terms directly attest to reliability; lower terms require additional verification.
4
Memorize the hierarchy of jarh terms
List terms from worst to least severe: kadhdhab, wadda', dajjal (worst); then saqit, dhahib, matruk; then raddu hadithihi, mutrah, laysa bi shay'; then da'if, munkar, wahin; then fihi maqal, laysa bi mardi, layyin.
The first categories indicate fisq and cannot be used even for i'tibar; lower categories may be used for i'tibar and mutaba'at.
5
Analyze the debate on multiple weak chains
Contrast the view in al-Tahrir (weak due to fisq cannot be strengthened by multiplicity) with Ibn al-Humam's comment (if the common element becomes mutawatir, even weak due to fisq becomes authoritative). Understand the conditions.
This ikhtilaf affects how Hanafi jurists evaluate hadith for istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: معرّف العدالة أمور منها (الشهرة) والتواتر (كمالك) الإمام (والأوزاعي و) عبد الله بن المبارك وغيرهم كالإمام الهمام أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه وبواقي أصحابه، والإمام الشافعي وأحمد بن حنبل وسائر الأئمة الكرام قدس سرهم لأنها فوق التزكية في إفادة العلم بالعدالة، (ولهذا) أي لأجل كون الشهرة فوق التزكية أنكر أحمد بن حنبل على من سأله عن إسحاق) ابن راهويه : هو عدل أم لا ؟ (و) أنكر يحيى بن معين على من سأله عن أبي عبيد فقال ابن معين (أبو عبيد يسأل عن الناس) وأنت تسأل عنه، يعني أنه مشهور بالعدالة حتى يجعل مزكياً وأنت عنه (و) منها (التزكية) وهي أخبار العدل بالعدالة، والأصل في مراتبها اصطلاح المزكي) ألفاظ التزكية ( والأشهر بين أهل الحديث أن أرفعها) في التعديل (حجة وثقة وحافظ ضابط) ثلاثتها توثيق للعدل فإن تلك الألفاظ ليست منبئة عن العدالة فلا بد من علمها بوجه آخر (ثم) بعدها ثلاثة ألفاظ (مأمون ، صدوق، لا بأس به، ثم بعدها (صالح، شيخ، حسن الحديث، صويلح و الأشهر في الجرح) أسوأها كذاب ، وضاع دجال ثم بعدها (ساقط، ذاهب، متروك، ومنه أي مما يلي المرتبة الأولى للبخاري فيه نظر، ثم بعدها (ردوا حديثه، مطرح، ليس بشيء، ففي هذه تزكية الجرح (لا حجية ولا تقوية) أي لا تصلح الرواية لهذا المجروح حجة في نفسه ولا يقوى غيره ولا يتقوى بغيره فيصير حجة (ثم) بعدها (ضعيف منكر الحديث واهِ، ثم بعدها فيه مقال ليس بمرضي لين ويصلح هذا للاعتبار والمتابعات) الاعتبار تتبع الأسانيد ليظهر للحديث ما يوافقه لفظاً أو معنى، من ذلك الصحابي الراوي أو غيره من الصحابة وهذا الموافق متابع له إن كان منه وشاهدان كان من غيره، وقد يطلقان مترادفين أيضاً، وإنما صلح هذا للاعتبار دون الأول، لأن المراتب الأول تدل على الفسق والفاسق لا يصلح حجة ولا مقوّياً ولا يصير بتقويته غيره حجة بحال بخلاف هذه، فإنها لا تدل على الفسق (و) قال في التحرير : حديث الراوي (الضعيف للفسق لا يرتقي بتعدد الطرق التي كلها ضعاف من الفسق إلى الحجية أصلاً، فإن خبر الفاسق لا يقبل بحال (و) حديث الراوي الضعيف (الغيره) أي لغير الفسق (مع العدالة ترتقي إلى الحجية، لأن العدالة موجبة لقبول خبره، وإنما كان الريبة بسوء الحفظ، وقد ارتفع بالتعدد، وبنى هو رحمه الله تعالى في فتح القدير على هذا الأصل مسائل كثيرة (أقول : التعدد قد يوجب تواتر القدر المشترك) كما (وحجيته غير مشروطة بالعدالة) فيكون خبر الضعاف للفسق متواتراً حجة، فَالضَّعِيفُ بِالْفِسْقِ وَغَيْرِهِ سَوَاءٌ (تَأَمَّلْ) وَلَعَلَّهُ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى أَرَادَ أَنَّ تَعَدُّدَ الطُّرُقِ بِحَيْثُ لَا يَخْرُجُ الْخَبَرُ عَنِ الْآحَادِيَّةِ يُوجِبُ الْحُجِّيَّةَ فِي الضَّعِيفِ بِغَيْرِ الْفِسْقِ دُونَ الضَّعِيفِ بِهِ وَأَمَّا الْمُتَوَاتِرُ فَخَارِجٌ عَنِ الْبَحْثِ بَلِ الْقَدْرُ الْمُشْتَرَكُ الَّذِي تَوَاتَرَ يُعْمَلُ بِهِ وَلَا يُعْمَلُ بِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ أَخْبَارِ الْآحَادِ، لِأَنَّ الْفِسْقَ مَانِعٌ وَمُوجِبٌ لِلتَّثَبُّتِ بِالنَّصِّ فَافْهَمْ
Issue: The definition of 'adala includes matters: (fame) and tawatur like (Malik) the Imam, (al-Awza'i), Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak and others such as the eminent Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions and the rest of his companions, and Imam al-Shafi'i and Ahmad ibn Hanbal and other noble imams, may Allah sanctify their souls, because they are above tazkiya in providing knowledge of 'adala. (For this reason), because fame is above tazkiya, Ahmad ibn Hanbal objected to the one who asked him about Ishaq ibn Rahawayh: 'Is he 'adil or not?' And Yahya ibn Ma'in objected to the one who asked him about Abu 'Ubayd, saying: 'Abu 'Ubayd asks about people, and you ask about him?' meaning that he is so famous for 'adala that he is considered a muzakki, while you ask about him. And (the definition of 'adala also includes) tazkiya, which is the report of an 'adil about 'adala. The principle in its ranks is the terminology of the muzakki. The most well-known among hadith experts is that the highest in ta'dil is: hujja, thiqah, hafiz, dabit – all three are documentation of the 'adil, for those terms are not indicative of 'adala by themselves, so it must be known through another means. Then after them, three terms: ma'mun, sadaq, la ba's bihi. Then after them: salih, shaykh, hasan al-hadith, suwaylih. And the most well-known in jarh: the worst is kadhdhab, wadda', dajjal. Then after them: saqit, dhahib, matruk, and from it (meaning what follows the first level) 'li al-Bukhari fihi nadhar'. Then after them: raddu hadithihi, mutrah, laysa bi shay'. In these there is tazkiyah of jarh (no authority and no strengthening) – that is, the narration of this majruh is neither a proof in itself nor does it strengthen others, nor is it strengthened by others to become a proof. Then after them: da'if, munkar al-hadith, wahin. Then after them: fihi maqal, laysa bi mardi, layyin. And this is suitable for i'tibar and mutaba'at. I'tibar is tracing the chains to see if a hadith has a similar wording or meaning from that sahabi narrator or from other sahaba; this similar narration is a mutaba'ah if from the same sahabi, and a shahid if from a different sahabi; sometimes they are used interchangeably. This category is suitable for i'tibar unlike the first categories, because the first categories indicate fisq, and the fasiq cannot serve as a proof nor strengthen nor be strengthened by others to become a proof at all, unlike these, which do not indicate fisq. And (the author) said in al-Tahrir: The hadith of a narrator who is weak due to fisq cannot be elevated to authority by multiple chains that are all weak due to fisq; the report of a fasiq is never accepted. And the hadith of a weak narrator (due to other reasons) – i.e., not for fisq – (with 'adala) is elevated to authority because 'adala mandates acceptance of his report, and the doubt was only due to poor memory, which is removed by multiplicity. And he (the author) built many issues on this principle in Fath al-Qadir. I say: Multiplicity may cause tawatur of the common element, and its authority is not conditioned by 'adala, so the report of those weak due to fisq could become mutawatir and thus authoritative. So the weak due to fisq and other than fisq are equal? Reflect. Perhaps he meant that multiplicity of chains that keeps the report within ahad status causes authority in the weak for other than fisq, but not in the weak due to fisq. As for mutawatir, it is outside the discussion; rather, the common element that becomes mutawatir is acted upon, but each individual ahad report is not acted upon because fisq is a preventer and requires verification by the text. So understand.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage defines the two methods for establishing 'adala: shuhra (fame) and tazkiya (explicit commendation). Shuhra is considered superior, exemplified by the great imams whom no one questions. Tazkiya is then elaborated with a hierarchy of terms used by hadith scholars. For ta'dil (praise), the highest terms are hujja, thiqah, hafiz, dabit; then ma'mun, sadaq, la ba's bihi; then lower terms like salih, shaykh. For jarh (criticism), the worst are kadhdhab, wadda', dajjal; then saqit, dhahib, matruk; then terms like raddu hadithihi, mutrah, laysa bi shay', which indicate such severity that the narrator cannot be used even as reinforcement. Lower levels like da'if, munkar al-hadith, wahin can be used for i'tibar and mutaba'at (seeking supporting chains). The passage then discusses the effect of multiple weak chains: those weak due to fisq cannot be strengthened by multiplicity unless they reach tawatur in the common element, while those weak due to other causes (like poor memory) can be strengthened if multiple weak chains concur. This is a nuanced Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الشهرة (al-shuhra): Widespread fame of the narrator's 'adala, considered stronger than tazkiya.
التزكية (al-tazkiya): Explicit commendation by an 'adil that another is 'adil.
الجرح (al-jarh): Criticism of a narrator's reliability, with varying degrees.
الاعتبار (al-i'tibar): Tracing chains to find supporting narrations; used for weak narrators not due to fisq.
المتابعات (al-mutaba'at): Supporting chains from the same companion (mutaba'ah) or different companion (shahid).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered the highest level of ta'dil?
A) صالح
B) صدوق
C) حجة وثقة وحافظ ضابط
D) لا بأس به

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul classification of narrator reliability is based on a clear hierarchy of ta'dil and jarh terms, with shuhra as the strongest proof of 'adala.

What Does Not Disqualify a Narrator: Key Exceptions
Enumerates acts and situations that do not invalidate a narrator's reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify six situations that do not constitute jarh and explain the Hanafi rationale for each.

Core Idea
Leaving action on a hadith, punishment for slander, or acting on ijtihad does not equate to unreliability.

This passage clarifies common misconceptions about narrator disqualification. Many assume that a narrator's personal practice must match his narration, but factors like abrogation, lack of witnesses, or legitimate scholarly disagreement prevent such conclusions. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for proper evaluation of narrators in hadith and testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factor
Read the passage and list each factor presented as not constituting jarh. Note: leaving practice of narration, punishment for slander, actions of ijtihad, lack of narration habit, single narrator, young age.
There are six distinct factors.
2
Understand the rationale
For each factor, locate the reason given in the text. For example, leaving practice may be due to abrogation; punishment for slander may be correct but lacking witnesses; ijtihad actions may be permissible in his own school.
The rationale typically involves possible valid excuses or lack of necessary conditions for jarh.
3
Examine the nuance
Note any conditions or limits mentioned. For actions of ijtihad, the text restricts it to when the person acts according to his own opinion; acting against his own view would be jarh. Similarly, for single narrator, the text mentions that some scholars require tazkiyyah from an imam.
These nuances show the Hanafi approach is not absolute but considers context.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a hypothetical narrator situation, determine whether the factor would constitute jarh in the Hanafi view. Use the rationale from the passage.
For example, a narrator who never narrates except from one source is not automatically jarh if he is 'adil and dabit.

ولا حرج بترك العمل في رواية أو شهادة) بترك الراوي أو الشاهد العمل، كما إذا كان الخبر محرماً فارتكبه أو موجباً فتركه، أو مبيحاً، فأفتى بالحرمة أو الوجوب، أو كان الشاهد حكماً أو قاضياً فلم يحكم بما شهد به (فلعل ثمة معارضاً لأجله ترك العمل أو علم بالنسخ فلا يدل على فسقه وأما أن هذا الخبر حجة أم لا فبحث آخر سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى (ولا) جرح أيضاً بحد بشهادة الزنا لعدم النصاب) لأنه يجوز أن يكون صادقاً فيما رمى به ولم يوافقه غيره فحد إلا أنه يرد عليه ما قالوا في تعليل عدم قبول شهادته أنه ارتكب جريمة إفشاء حال المسلم مع عدم حسبة إقامة الحد باللسان فجوزي بعدم قبول قوله فإنه يدل على كونه فاسقاً فتأمل فيه (ولا) جرح أيضاً (بالأفعال المجتهد فيها) كاللعب بالشطرنج من غير قمار وشرب المثلث، وأكل متروك التسمية عامداً، فإنه معصية عند رؤيتها مباحة، وقد نقل عن الشافعي في شارب المثلث أحدبه وأقبل شهادته، لكن العدالة والضبط ولا يخل شيئاً منهما ، وأيضاً أن زبيراً رضي الله تعالى عنه لم يكن معتاداً بها وكذا ،بلال ومن ههنا ظهر بطلان قول بعض المتعصبين في حق الإمام الهمام الشهير بالشرق والغرب الإمام أبي حنيفة الكوفي رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه ضعيف لكونه غير معتاد بالرواية وأيضاً قالوا: إنه قد أخذ دفتر شيخه حماد رضي الله تعالى عنه فيروي منه، انظر بعين الإنصاف أي طعن في هذا؟ فإن الرواية عن المكتوب آية كمال الاحتياط والورع وخوف الله تعالى (ولا) جرح أيضاً بأن له راوياً واحداً (فقط) دون غيره؟ (وهو مجهول العين باصطلاح) كسمعان ليس له راوِ غير الشعبي فإن المناط العدالة والحفظ لا تعدد الرواة، وقيل: لا يقبل عند أكثر المحدثين وهو تحكم وقيل : إن كان عادة هذا المنفرد النقل من الثقة يقبل، وقيل: إن زكاه أحد من الأئمة يقبل، وهذا قريب من المختار (ولا) أيضاً بحداثة السن) لعدم دخل السن فيما هو أيضاً (بالتدليس بإيهام الرواية عن المعاصر الأعلى) وهو يرويه عن الأدنى المشارك له في الاسم أو اللقب بالسماع عنه لقيه أولاً (أو) التدليس (بذكر شيخه بأسماء لإيهام العلو) أي لإيهام أن شيخه عال (أو) لإيهام (لكثرة) أي لإيهام أن شيوخه أكثر، وعدم الجرح بهذين التدليسين إنما هو على الأصح من المذاهب، وذهب كثير من المحدثين إلى أن التدليس جارح وحجة عدم الجرح بأنه لا معصية لعدم الكذب (لكنه) أي التدليس (مكروه) وجه الكراهة ظاهر، ومن يرى التدليس جارحاً يراه معصية كبيرة، حتى قال بعض أهل الحديث : لأن أزني خير من أن أدلس ولا بد من إثبات كونه كبيرة بدليل إذ لا دخل فيه للرأي، وأما الحديث الذي وقع فيه التدليس هل هو حجة أم لا فالأكثر من المحدثين
And there is no objection (jarh) due to leaving (acting upon) a narration or testimony – i.e., the narrator or witness leaving action upon it, as when a hadith is prohibitive and he engages in that act, or obligatory and he leaves it, or permissible and he gives a fatwa of prohibition or obligation, or when the witness is a judge or ruler and does not judge by what he witnessed. Perhaps there is a counterevidence causing him to leave the action, or he knew of abrogation; thus it does not indicate his fisq. As to whether this hadith is authoritative or not is another discussion. And there is no jarh due to being flogged for false accusation of zina due to insufficient witnesses (nassab), because he might have been truthful in his accusation but no one else corroborated it, so he was flogged. But there is a rebuttal: the reason his testimony is not accepted is that he committed the crime of disclosing a Muslim's affair without seeking to establish the hadd by tongue; thus he was punished by non-acceptance of his statement, which indicates fisq. Reflect on that. And there is no jarh due to actions subject to ijtihad, such as playing chess without gambling, drinking nabidh al-muthallath, and eating meat on which the basmala was deliberately omitted. These are sinful according to some but permissible according to others. It is narrated that al-Shafi'i drank muthallath and yet his testimony was accepted. However, this should be restricted to when the person acts according to his own opinion; if he acts against his own view of prohibition, then it should not be accepted, e.g., a Hanafi eating meat on which basmala was omitted on purpose, or a Shafi'i drinking muthallath. And there is no jarh due to not being accustomed to narration, because the criteria for acceptance are 'adala and dabit, and lack of habit does not harm them. Moreover, Zubayr (ra) was not accustomed to narration, nor was Bilal. From this emerges the invalidity of the claim of some bigots against the eminent Imam Abu Hanifa that he is weak because he was not accustomed to narration. And they also said: he took the notebook of his shaykh Hammad (ra) and narrated from it. Look with fairness: what criticism is this? Narrating from written records is the epitome of caution, piety, and fear of Allah. And there is no jarh due to having only a single narrator (which makes him unknown by name in terminology), like Sham'an who has no narrator other than al-Sha'bi; the criterion is 'adala and memory, not multiplicity of narrators. It has been said that he is not accepted according to most muhaddithin, but that is arbitrary. Some said: if this single narrator habitually transmits from trustworthy people, he is accepted. Some said: if one of the imams declares him trustworthy, he is accepted. This last is close to the chosen opinion. And there is no jarh due to young age, because age does not affect the criteria. Nor due to tadlis by implying narration from a higher contemporary while actually narrating from a lower one sharing the same name or kunya, having heard from him first. Or tadlis by mentioning his shaykh with multiple names to imply high chains (i.e., to imply that his shaykh is high) or to imply many shuyukh. The absence of jarh for these two types of tadlis is according to the most authentic opinion; many muhaddithin consider tadlis as jarh. The argument for no jarh is that there is no sin because there is no lie. However, tadlis is makruh (disliked). Those who consider tadlis as jarh see it as major sin, so much so that some hadith scholars said: 'Committing zina is better than tadlis.' But it must be proven to be a major sin by evidence, as it is not based on opinion. Regarding the hadith in which tadlis occurs, whether it is authoritative or not, most muhaddithin... (the text ends).
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage lists several factors that do not constitute jarh (disqualification) of a narrator or witness. It addresses common misconceptions such as: leaving the practice of a narration does not imply the narrator is unreliable because there may be valid reasons (like abrogation or counterevidence). Similarly, being punished for slander (without enough witnesses) does not automatically make one a fasiq if the accusation was truthful. Actions subject to ijtihad (like playing chess or drinking certain liquids) are not grounds for jarh if the person acts according to his own school. Not being a frequent narrator does not harm one's reliability; even great companions like Zubayr and Bilal did not narrate often. Having only one transmitter also does not necessarily disqualify; the focus is on 'adala and memory. Youth, tadlis (by name ambiguity), and certain types of tadlis that do not involve lying are not jarh, though tadlis is disliked. The passage ends with a discussion on tadlis and authority of such hadith. The Hanafi position generally treats these factors as non-jarh, with the most authentic opinion as stated.

Key Terms
الجرح (al-jarh): Disqualification of a narrator due to defects impairing 'adala or memory.
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing the identity of a shaykh or using ambiguous names to give a false impression of a higher chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is being flogged for false accusation of zina not considered jarh in the Hanafi view?
A) Because the flogging may have been unjust.
B) Because the narrator might have been truthful but lacked witnesses.
C) Because false accusation of zina is not a major sin.
D) Because flogging is a valid punishment only for zina.

Key Takeaway
Six common factors – leaving practice, punishment for slander, ijtihadi acts, lack of narration habit, single narrator, youth – are not grounds for jarh in Hanafi usul because they do not undermine 'adala or dabit when properly contextualized.

Tadlis: When Does Concealment Become Jarh?
Enumerates acts and situations that do not invalidate a narrator's reliability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between types of tadlis and state the Hanafi ruling that non-lying tadlis is not jarh but makruh.

Core Idea
Tadlis without lying is not jarh, but it is makruh and requires cautious acceptance.

The passage concludes with a discussion of tadlis (concealment) in hadith transmission. While many muhaddithin consider any tadlis a jarh, the Hanafi school distinguishes between lying tadlis and mere ambiguity. This lesson unpacks that distinction and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Define the two types of tadlis
The text mentions: (1) tadlis by implying narration from a higher contemporary while actually using a lower one sharing the same name, (2) tadlis by mentioning the shaykh with multiple names to imply high chains or many shuyukh. Identify each.
Both involve no outright lie.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
The text states that these types are not jarh according to the most authentic opinion (على الأصح من المذاهب). The reason: there is no sin because there is no lie. Criteria for acceptance are 'adala and dabit.
Hanafis focus on the absence of falsehood.
3
Examine the opposing view
Many muhaddithin see any tadlis as a major sin, even quoting 'committing zina is better than tadlis'. Their reasoning: deception can lead to misleading chains.
This opposition is strong, but the text challenges it on the basis of evidence.
4
Note the nuancing: makruh
The text says tadlis is makruh, acknowledging the unease. It also notes that the authority of a hadith with tadlis is a separate discussion.
Makruh means not sinful but disliked.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a narrator uses a common name to obscure that he heard from a lower shaykh, is he accepted? Hanafi: yes, but makruh. He remains 'adil and dabit.
Practical difference: narrations from such a person are still considered, but with caution.

It addresses common misconceptions such as: leaving the practice of a narration does not imply the narrator is unreliable because there may be valid reasons (like abrogation or counterevidence). Key Terms
الجرح (al-jarh): Disqualification of a narrator due to defects impairing 'adala or memory.
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing the identity of a shaykh or using ambiguous names to give a false impression of a higher chain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on tadlis that involves using a similar name to imply a higher chain?
A) It is a major sin and jarh.
B) It is not jarh but it is makruh.
C) It is acceptable and not disliked.
D) It is jarh only if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, tadlis that does not involve lying is not jarh, though it is makruh; the narrator remains acceptable if 'adil and dabit, but caution is advised.

Three Non-Jarh Factors in Narrator Reliability
Rulings on actions that do not discredit a narrator

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three actions that do not constitute jarh in Hanafi usul and explain why actions based on valid ijtihad do not discredit a narrator.

Core Idea
Leaving a narration, hadd punishment, or ijtihadi acts do not automatically discredit a narrator.

The reliability of narrators and witnesses is paramount in Islamic law. However, certain actions might appear sinful but, in the Hanafi view, do not necessarily indicate lack of 'adala. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut examines three such scenarios, emphasizing the reasoning that prevents automatic discrediting. Understanding these exceptions is essential for proper evaluation of narrators and the application of usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Scenarios
Locate the three cases mentioned in the passage: leaving action on a narration, being flogged for false accusation of zina due to insufficient witnesses, and performing actions subject to ijtihad.
The text marks each with 'لا' (nor) after the initial 'ولا حرج'.
2
Analyze the Reasoning (Talil) for Each
For each scenario, extract the reason why it does not necessarily indicate sin. Note the use of 'لعل' (perhaps) and 'يجوز' (it is possible) showing uncertainty or valid excuse.
Focus on the principle that an action may have a valid justification.
3
Differentiate Between Ijtihad and Violation
Understand the crucial nuance: acting according to one's own valid ijtihad is not sinful, but acting against one's own belief of prohibition is. The passage gives examples of Hanafi and Shafi'i cases.
This is key to the Hanafi position on 'af'al mujtahad fiha.
4
Recognize Cross-Madhhab Nuance
Note that some scholars (like al-Shafi'i) might punish the drinker of muthallath yet still accept his testimony, showing that punishment alone does not equate to jarh.
The text itself reports this, indicating it is not necessarily contradictory.
5
Apply the Principle to a New Scenario
Given a new case (e.g., a Hanafi narrator who plays chess for entertainment without gambling), determine whether it constitutes jarh based on the rule that ijtihadi acts do not discredit.
Recall that the action must be permissible in the narrator's own school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا حرج بترك العمل في رواية أو شهادة) بترك الراوي أو الشاهد العمل، كما إذا كان الخبر محرماً فارتكبه أو موجباً فتركه، أو مبيحاً، فأفتى بالحرمة أو الوجوب، أو كان الشاهد حكماً أو قاضياً فلم يحكم بنا شهد به (فلعل ثمة معارضاً لأجله ترك العمل أو علم بالنسخ فلا يدل على فسقه وأما أن هذا الخبر حجة أم لا فبحث آخر سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى (ولا) جرح أيضاً بحد بشهادة الزنا لعدم النصاب) لأنه يجوز أن يكون صادقاً فيما رمى به ولم يوافقه غيره فحد إلا أنه يرد عليه ما قالوا في تعليل عدم قبول شهادته أنه ارتكب جريمة إفشاء حال المسلم مع عدم حسبة إقامة الحد باللسان فجوزي بعدم قبول قوله فإنه يدل على كونه فاسقاً فتأمل فيه (ولا) جرح أيضاً (بالأفعال المجتهد فيها) كاللعب بالشطرنج من غير قمار وشرب المثلث، وأكل متروك التسمية عامداً، فإنه معصية عند رؤيتها مباحة، وقد نقل عن الشافعي في شارب المثلث أحدبه وأقبل شهادته، لكن ينبغي تقييد المسألة بما إذا عمل موافقاً لرأيه، وأما إذا ارتكب بها رائياً للحرمة فينبغي أن لا يقبل كحنفي أكل متروك التسمية وشافعي شرب المثلث
And there is no problem with leaving action upon a narration or testimony: by the narrator or witness leaving action, such as if the report is prohibitive and he violates it, or mandatory and he leaves it, or permissive and he gives a fatwa of prohibition or obligation, or if the witness is a ruler or judge and does not judge according to what he testified. (Perhaps there is a countervailing reason for leaving action or he knows of abrogation, so it does not indicate his sinfulness. And as for whether this report is a proof or not, that is another investigation to come, God willing.) And nor is there discrediting also by being flogged for the testimony of zina due to lack of the required number of witnesses: because it is possible that he was truthful in what he accused and no one else supported him, so he was flogged. Except that it is objected against them what they said in the reasoning for not accepting his testimony: that he committed the crime of exposing the condition of a Muslim without the intention of establishing the legal punishment by speech, so he was penalized by not accepting his statement, and this indicates his sinfulness; so ponder on that. And nor is there discrediting also by actions subject to ijtihad, such as playing chess without gambling, drinking al-muthallath, and intentionally eating meat over which the basmala was omitted; for it is disobedience according to those who see it as permissible. And it is reported from al-Shafi'i about the drinker of al-muthallath that he flogged him and accepted his testimony. But the issue should be restricted to when he acts according to his own opinion. As for if he commits it while believing it is forbidden, then he should not be accepted, like a Hanafi eating meat over which the basmala was omitted and a Shafi'i drinking al-muthallath.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage (a ruling with reasoning) addresses three scenarios that might seem to discredit a narrator or witness but do not necessarily do so. First, if a narrator or witness leaves acting on his own narration or testimony, this does not automatically make him a fasiq, as there may be a valid excuse (e.g., a countervailing evidence or knowledge of abrogation). Second, if a person is flogged for falsely accusing someone of zina due to insufficient witnesses, this does not discredit him because he might have been truthful but lacked the required witnesses; however, some argue that the act itself shows sinfulness. Third, actions that are subject to ijtihad—meaning scholars differ on their permissibility—do not discredit a narrator if he acts according to his own ijtihad. For example, a Hanafi who eats meat without basmalah considering it permissible is not discredited, but if he believes it is forbidden and still does it, he is a fasiq and rejected. The passage emphasizes that these actions do not necessarily indicate lack of 'adala.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): A defect that discredits a narrator's reliability in hadith or testimony
الأفعال المجتهد فيها (al-af'al al-mujtahad fiha): Actions on which scholars differ regarding permissibility, such as playing chess without gambling or drinking certain liquids

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following actions does NOT discredit a narrator?
A) Leaving action on a narration due to possible abrogation
B) Being flogged for false accusation of zina with insufficient witnesses
C) Playing chess without gambling as a Hanafi following his school's permissibility
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Actions based on valid ijtihad do not constitute jarh, and leaving a narration or being flogged for hadd does not automatically indicate sinfulness.

Non-Jarh Factors: Lack of Habit, Single Narrator, Young Age
Enumeration of non-discrediting factors in narrator criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain why three specific factors (lack of habit, single narration, young age) do not discredit a narrator according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A narrator is not discredited by lack of habit, having only one narrator, or young age; the criteria are integrity and accuracy.

In the previous lesson, we studied factors that do discredit a narrator (jarh). Now we continue with factors that do not. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut explains why lack of habit, having only one narrator, and young age are not valid grounds for rejection. Understanding this helps us properly evaluate hadith narrators and appreciate the Hanafi approach to narrator criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify each non-jarh factor
List the three factors the passage presents: lack of habit in narration, having only one narrator (majhul al-ayn), and young age. Recognize that these are common misconceptions in narrator criticism.
Each factor is introduced with 'ولا جرح أيضاً'.
2
Extract the reasoning for each factor
For each factor, find the textual reasoning. For lack of habit: the requirement is 'adala and dhabt, not frequency. For single narrator: the criterion is integrity and memory, not multiplicity. For young age: age does not affect integrity or memory.
The passage uses Companions (Zubayr, Bilal) and defends Imam Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyze the defense of Imam Abu Hanifa
The text rebuts the claim that Imam Abu Hanifa is weak due to lack of habit. It notes that he narrated from his teacher's notebook, which shows caution and piety. This illustrates how the principle applies to a major figure.
This is an example of applying the rule to defend a scholar.
4
Evaluate the opinions on majhul al-ayn
The passage presents multiple views: (1) most hadith scholars reject, (2) accepted if the solitary narrator habitually transmits from trustworthy sources, (3) accepted if an imam declares him reliable (the preferred view). Understand why the Hanafi school favors the third view.
The preferred view ('al-mukhtar') ties acceptance to a trustworthy source's declaration.
5
Summarize the Hanafi usul principle
Conclude that these factors do not discredit because the core requirements are 'adala and dhabt, which are independent of habit, number of narrators, and age. This is a key Hanafi principle in narrator criticism.
Memorize: 'المناط العدالة والضبط'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( ولا ) جرح أيضاً بعدم اعتياد الرواية) فإن الموجب للقبول العدالة والضبط ولا يخل شيئاً منهما ، وأيضاً أن زبيراً رضي الله تعالى عنه لم يكن معتاداً بها وكذا ،بلال ومن ههنا ظهر بطلان قول بعض المتعصبين في حق الإمام الهمام الشهير بالشرق والغرب الإمام أبي حنيفة الكوفي رضي الله تعالى عنه أنه ضعيف لكونه غير معتاد بالرواية وأيضاً قالوا: إنه قد أخذ دفتر شيخه حماد رضي الله تعالى عنه فيروي منه، انظر بعين الإنصاف أي طعن في هذا؟ فإن الرواية عن المكتوب آية كمال الاحتياط والورع وخوف الله تعالى (ولا) جرح أيضاً بأن له راوياً واحداً (فقط) دون غيره؟ (وهو مجهول العين باصطلاح) كسمعان ليس له راوِ غير الشعبي فإن المناط العدالة والحفظ لا تعدد الرواة، وقيل: لا يقبل عند أكثر المحدثين وهو تحكم وقيل : إن كان عادة هذا المنفرد النقل من الثقة يقبل، وقيل: إن زكاه أحد من الأئمة يقبل، وهذا قريب من المختار (ولا) أيضاً بحداثة السن) لعدم دخل السن فيما هو أيضاً
And nor is there discrediting also by not being accustomed to narration: for what necessitates acceptance is integrity and accuracy, and nothing is lacking from them. Also, Zubayr (may God be pleased with him) was not accustomed to narration, and likewise Bilal. From this emerges the invalidity of the claim of some bigots regarding the great imam famous in the east and west, Imam Abu Hanifa al-Kufi (may God be pleased with him), that he is weak for not being accustomed to narration. Also, they said: He took the notebook of his teacher Hammad (may God be pleased with him) and narrated from it. Look with an eye of fairness: what criticism is in this? For narration from writing is a sign of complete caution, piety, and fear of God. And nor is there discrediting also by him having only one narrator, (only) without others? (And he is majhul al-ayn in terminology) like Sam'an who has no narrator other than al-Sha'bi, for the criterion is integrity and retention, not multiplicity of narrators. And it is said: He is not accepted according to most hadith scholars, and that is arbitrary. And it is said: If the habit of this solitary narrator is to transmit from trustworthy sources, he is accepted. And it is said: If one of the imams declares him reliable, he is accepted, and this is close to the chosen view. And nor also by young age: because age has no bearing on that which is also...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage (a ruling with reasoning) continues enumerating factors that do not constitute jarh (discrediting). First, lack of habit in narrating hadith does not discredit a narrator, as many Companions like Zubayr and Bilal narrated little. The text uses this to defend Imam Abu Hanifa against claims that he was weak due to not being a prolific narrator; rather, his use of written materials shows caution. Second, having only one narrator (being majhul al-ayn) is not in itself a defect, as the standard is 'adala and dhabt, not multiple narrators. The text discusses different opinions: some reject such narrators, but the preferred view (al-mukhtar) is that if a trustworthy source declares him reliable, he is accepted. Third, young age does not discredit a narrator, as age does not affect integrity or memory.

Key Terms
عدم اعتياد الرواية (adam i'tiyad al-riwaya): Not being accustomed to narrating many hadith
مجهول العين (majhul al-ayn): A narrator who has only one person narrating from him, thus unknown by identity to most scholars
العدالة والضبط (al-'adala wa al-dhabt): Integrity and accuracy — the two core requirements for narrator acceptance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Multiplicity of narrators reporting from him
B) Being accustomed to narrating many hadiths
C) Integrity and accuracy (al-'adala wa al-dhabt)
D) Being of mature age

Key Takeaway
Lack of habit, having only one narrator, and young age do not discredit a narrator; the decisive factors are integrity and accuracy.

Tadlis: Types and Impact on Narrator Reliability in Hanafi Usul
Explaining tadlis and its impact on narrator credibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of tadlis, apply the Hanafi position on their impact on narrator credibility, and evaluate the dispute with the muhaddithun.

Core Idea
Tadlis without lying does not discredit a narrator; his narration is suspended until verified.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut tackles a key issue in hadith criticism: tadlis (concealing a defect in the chain). The Hanafi school takes a nuanced view: not all tadlis is jarh, only certain forms and under specific conditions. We will explore the three types mentioned, the soundest Hanafi ruling, and the opposing view that considers tadlis a major sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of tadlis
From the text, list: (1) tadlis by implying narration from a higher contemporary, (2) tadlis by mentioning the shaykh with multiple names to imply elevation, and (3) tadlis al-taswiya (dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones).
The first two are sometimes considered less severe.
2
Determine the Hanafi ruling on each type
For types 1 and 2, the soundest opinion (al-ashah) is that they are not jarh, only makruh. For type 3, the ruling depends on one's stance on mursal hadith.
The passage explicitly states 'the absence of discrediting by these two types of tadlis is according to the soundest of madhhabs'.
3
Analyze the proof for the Hanafi position
The Hanafi dalil is the absence of explicit lying (kizb). Tadlis is concealment, not falsehood. Even the saying 'lianna azni khayr min an adallis' is not considered a decisive proof for it being a major sin.
The text notes that if tadlis were a major sin, it must be proven by evidence, not mere opinion.
4
Examine the opposing view and its basis
Many muhaddithun consider tadlis as jarh and a major sin. They rely on the principle that deception violates trust, and some use the saying mentioned above.
The thamarah al-khilaf is whether a mudallis's hadith is accepted or rejected.
5
Apply the rule to a mudallis's narration
The correct view is suspension (tawaqquf) of judgment on his hadith until his true reliability is clarified. This is not rejection, but caution.
The text says: 'the correct is suspension regarding his hadith until the reality of the situation appears'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(بالتدليس بإيهام الرواية عن المعاصر الأعلى) وهو يرويه عن الأدنى المشارك له في الاسم أو اللقب بالسماع عنه لقيه أولاً (أو) التدليس (بذكر شيخه بأسماء لإيهام العلو) أي لإيهام أن شيخه عال (أو) لإيهام (لكثرة) أي لإيهام أن شيوخه أكثر، وعدم الجرح بهذين التدليسين إنما هو على الأصح من المذاهب، وذهب كثير من المحدثين إلى أن التدليس جارح وحجة عدم الجرح بأنه لا معصية لعدم الكذب (لكنه) أي التدليس (مكروه) وجه الكراهة ظاهر، ومن يرى التدليس جارحاً يراه معصية كبيرة، حتى قال بعض أهل الحديث : لأن أزني خير من أن أدلس ولا بد من إثبات كونه كبيرة بدليل إذ لا دخل فيه للرأي، وأما الحديث الذي وقع فيه التدليس هل هو حجة أم لا فالأكثر من المحدثين لا، إلا إذا علم حال الراوي الذي وقع فيه التدليس، وقيل: هذا مبني على أن رواية الثقة توثيق أم لا، وفي كون رواية المدلس توثيقاً تأمل ( وأما ) التدليس بإسقاط ضعيف) وهو قوي عنده (من بين ثقتين وبعبارة أخرى : إسقاط مختلف فيه اعتماداً على كونه ثقة (وهو) تدليس التسوية فيضر عند نفاة المراسيل ،حجيتها، وأما عند من يقبل المراسيل فيقبل، لأن جزمه بالرواية توثيق للمسقط، كما في المرسل، لكن قبول إرسال المدلس لا يخلو عن (والصحيح عدم سقوطه أي سقوط هذا المدلس (العدم) صريح (الكذب) بل غاية ما فعل الرواية عن المجهول ولا غائبة فيها (بل) الصحيح (التوقف) في حديثه حتى يظهر حقيقة الحال، ثم تدليس التسوية إنما يكون إذا كان من بعد المسقط معاصراً وإلا فلا تدليس فافهم
(By tadlis of implying narration from a higher contemporary) meaning he narrates from a lower narrator who shares his name or epithet, claiming he heard from him first. (Or) tadlis (by mentioning his shaykh with names to imply elevation) meaning to imply that his shaykh is higher. (Or) to imply (multiplicity) meaning to imply that his shuyukh are many. And the absence of discrediting by these two types of tadlis is only according to the soundest of the madhhabs. And many of the muhaddithun went that tadlis is a defect, and the proof of no defect is that there is no disobedience due to absence of lying, (but it) i.e. tadlis (is makruh). The reason for karaha is apparent. And whoever sees tadlis as a defect regards it as a major sin, even some hadith scholars said: For me to commit zina is better than for me to do tadlis. And it is necessary to prove it is a major sin by evidence, since there is no room for opinion. As for the hadith in which tadlis occurred, is it a proof or not? Most muhaddithun say no, except when the condition of the narrator who did tadlis is known. And it is said: This is based on whether the narration of a trustworthy person is a form of tawthiq or not. And there is consideration in whether the narration of a mudallis is tawthiq. (And as for) tadlis by dropping a weak (narrator) who is strong in his view (from between two trustworthy ones) in other words: dropping one who is differed about, relying on his being trustworthy, (and it is) tadlis al-taswiya. It harms according to those who reject the mursal as proof. As for those who accept mursal, they accept, because his certainty of narration is a tawthiq of the dropped one, as in mursal. But accepting the mursal of the mudallis is not free from... (And the correct is that he is not fallen) i.e. the falling of this mudallis (is not) explicit lying. Rather the utmost he did was narrating from an unknown, and there is no issue in that. (Rather) the correct (is suspension) regarding his hadith until the reality of the situation appears. Then tadlis al-taswiya occurs only if the one after the dropped one is a contemporary, otherwise there is no tadlis; so understand.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage (a ruling with reasoning) discusses tadlis (concealing defects in isnad) and whether it discredits a narrator. It identifies three types: (1) tadlis by implying narration from a higher contemporary (isnad al-‘ali), (2) tadlis by mentioning the shaykh with multiple names to imply elevation, and (3) tadlis by dropping a weak narrator (tadlis al-taswiya). For the first two, the soundest opinion (al-ashah) is that they do not discredit the narrator, though they are makruh. Many muhaddithun consider tadlis as jarh, even a major sin. The authenticity of hadith of a mudallis is debated; most do not accept unless his condition is known. Tadlis al-taswiya (dropping a weak link between two trustworthy narrators) is harmful according to those who reject mursal, but acceptable to those who accept mursal. The correct view is that the narrator is not discredited (his hadith is not rejected outright) but his narration is suspended until verified.

Key Terms
تدليس (tadlis): Concealing a defect in the isnad to make it appear stronger
تدليس التسوية (tadlis al-taswiya): Dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones to make the chain appear sound
تدليس بإيهام الرواية عن المعاصر الأعلى (tadlis bi iham al-riwaya 'an al-mu'asir al-a'la): Tadlis by implying narration from a higher contemporary
تدليس بذكر شيخه بأسماء لإيهام العلو (tadlis bi dhikr shaykhihi bi asma li iham al-'ulu): Tadlis by mentioning the shaykh with multiple names to imply elevation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct view regarding the hadith of a mudallis (one who does tadlis)?
A) It is always rejected
B) It is always accepted
C) His narration is suspended until his condition is known
D) It is accepted only if he is a sahabi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that tadlis without explicit lying does not discredit a narrator; his hadith is suspended until his reliability is clarified.

Indicators of 'Adala and the Hanafi Position on the Silence of the Salaf
Identifying what establishes a narrator's integrity and responding to objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three mu'arrafat al-'adala, apply the Hanafi rule of sukt al-salaf to narrator evaluation, and critique the objection that this is a case of ta'dil over jarh.

Core Idea
The silence of the Salaf about a narrator strongly indicates his integrity; acting on his report is tawthiq, not ta'dil.

This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' explains three indicators of narrator integrity: a judge's ruling, a mujtahid's action, and the silence of the Salaf. The Hanafi school uniquely holds that silence implies acceptance, and the Fatima bint Qais incident illustrates how this differs from other approaches. The text also refutes the claim that this is a mere application of giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three mu'arrafat al-'adala
List the three indicators mentioned: (1) a judge's ruling based on testimony, (2) a mujtahid's action on a narration, and (3) the silence of the Salaf when the narration is widespread.
Each indicator requires that the judge/mujtahid himself be 'adil and that no other basis exists.
2
Analyze the Hanafi position on sukt al-salaf
The Salaf, due to their integrity, would not remain silent about a criticized narrator. Their silence thus indicates acceptance. However, if they differ (some accept, some reject), the narrator is still considered 'known' (ka'l-ma'ruf). If only criticism appears, he is rejected. If nothing appears, acting on his report is permissible, especially in supererogatory matters.
This is a nuanced position: not absolute acceptance, but a gradient.
3
Examine the Fatima bint Qais example
Fatima narrated that the Prophet did not assign her maintenance or lodging after a final divorce. 'Umar rejected it, but Aisha explained it was due to the absence of a secure house. The Hanafis accept this hadith as evidence, showing that rejection by a single Companion does not discredit the narrator.
The example demonstrates that 'adala is established despite one critic, because other factors (like the reason for the ruling) may explain the criticism.
4
Discuss the status of unknown Sahabis
The rule of 'adala applies only to Sahabis of long companionship; those who accompanied briefly or are unknown may not be automatically 'udul. The Hanafis investigate their status.
This refutes the idea that all Sahabis are automatically 'udul without exception.
5
Refute al-Badi's claim of ta'dil over jarh
Al-Badi claimed that accepting the narrator here is giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh. The author responds: acting on the report is tawthiq (declaring trustworthy), not ta'dil, and leaving action is not jarh—it may be due to stronger counter-evidence.
This clarifies the epistemological basis: the Hanafis do not simply prefer ta'dil over jarh; they use contextual indicators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ومن المعرفات) للعدالة حكم الحاكم أي القاضي إذا حكم بشهادته (وعمل المجتهد) براويته، لكن لا مطلقاً، بل حال كونهما عدلين (شارطين للعدالة) وهذا إذا لم يكن له مستند آخر ولا يكون هو ثالث الشهداء (و) من المعرفات أيضاً (سكوت السلف) عن الطعن (عند اشتهار روايته إذ لا يسكتون) بعدالتهم على منكر) والعمل بخبر المطعون منكر، لكن هذا عند الاستطاعة فإن قبله بعض من السلف ورده بعض فكثير من أهل الحديث (على الرد والحنفية على القبول فإنهم قالوا الراوي إن كان غير معروف بالفقاهة ولا بالرواية بل إنما عرف بحديث أو حديثين فإن قبله الأئمة وسكتوا عنه عند ظهور الرواية أو اختلفوا كان كالمعروف وإن لم يظهر منهم غير الطعن كان مردوداً وإن لم يظهر شيء منهم لم يجب العمل، بل يجوز، أن قائلاً: فيعمل به في المندوبات والفضائل والتواريخ ومثلوا المطعون بفاطمة بنت قيس فإنها روت زوجها طلق فبت الطلاق، فلم يجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لها نفقة وسكنى وقال : اعتدي في بيت ابن أم مكتوم فإنه رجل أعمى فردها أمير المؤمنين عمر لا نترك كتاب ربنا وسنة نبينا بقول امرأة لا ندري أصدقت أم كذبت، حفظت أم نسيت، وأم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله تعالى عنها قائلة : ألا تتقي الله تعالى، إنما أمرها بالاعتداد في بيت ابن أم مكتوم لأنه لم يكن لزوجها بيت غير ما هو عورة ومعنى ما ذكرنا ثابت في صحيح مسلم»، فإن قلت يظهر من كلامهم أن الحكم عام في الراوي مطلقاً، صحابياً كان أو غيره كما تدل الأمثلة والصحابة كلهم عدول فلا وجه لرد رواية الغير المعروف من الصحابة، وإن تكلم عليه البعض قلت سيجيء أن حكم العدالة إنما هو في الصحابي الذي طالت صحبته وكون هذا المجهول منه محل بحث بل طويل الصحبة إما فقيه أو معروف بالرواية، نعم يرد على من سمى الصحابي لمن صحب ولو ساعة، مع أن الصحبة أيضاً محل بحث، ولا يلزم من المعاصرة أو الاجتماع في بلد الصحبة فافهم، ولما كان مزعوم صاحب البديع أن هذا من باب تقديم التعديل على الجرح لأن الرد لأجل جرح في الراوي والقبول للتعديل مع التقديم للجرح كما سيجيء إن شاء الله تعالى أراد إزالة هذا الزعم وقال: (وليس) هذا (من) باب (تقديم التعديل على الجرح (كما) زعم (في البديع بل العمل) بخبره (توثيق) له فإن عمل المجتهد توثيق (والترك) لعمل ليس بجرح لجواز أن يكون لوجدان معارض أقوى أو مساو أو
(And from the indicators) of integrity: the ruling of a hakim, i.e., the judge, if he rules based on his testimony; (and the action of a mujtahid) by narrating from him, but not absolutely, rather while both are just (stipulating integrity). And this is when there is no other basis and he is not the third of the witnesses. (And) from the indicators also (the silence of the Salaf) from criticism (when his narration is widespread, for they do not remain silent) due to their integrity (upon evil). Acting upon the report of a criticized person is evil, but this is when possible. For if some of the Salaf accepted it and others rejected it, then many of the hadith scholars are for rejection, and the Hanafis are for acceptance. For they said: The narrator, if he is not known for fiqh nor for narration but only known by one or two hadith, then if the imams accepted him and remained silent about him when his narration appeared, or they differed, he is like a known one. And if nothing other than criticism appears from them, he is rejected. And if nothing appears from them, acting on it is not obligatory, but permissible (such that it is acted upon in supererogatory matters, virtues, and histories). And they cited as an example the criticized: Fatima bint Qais, for she narrated that her husband divorced her with a final divorce, and the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and Companions) did not assign her maintenance or lodging, and said: 'Observe your waiting period in the house of Ibn Umm Maktum, for he is a blind man.' So the Commander of the Faithful, Umar, rejected it, saying: 'We do not abandon the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the saying of a woman; we do not know if she is truthful or lying, if she remembered or forgot.' And the Mother of the Believers, Aisha al-Siddiqa (may God be pleased with him) said: 'Do you not fear God? He only ordered her to observe her waiting period in the house of Ibn Umm Maktum because her husband did not have a house other than one that was exposed.' And the meaning of what we mentioned is confirmed in Sahih Muslim. For if you say: It appears from their speech that the ruling is general for the narrator absolutely, whether a Sahabi or otherwise, as the examples indicate, and all Sahabis are trustworthy, so there is no reason to reject the narration of an unknown among the Sahabis, even if some criticized him. I say: It will come that the rule of integrity applies only to the Sahabi whose companionship was long, and this unknown being from them is a matter of investigation. Rather, a long-standing companion is either a faqih or known for narration. Yes, it is refuted against whoever calls a Sahabi one who accompanied even for a moment, while companionship itself is also a matter of investigation. And contemporaneity or meeting in a country does not necessitate companionship; so understand. And since the claimant of al-Badi' claimed that this is from the chapter of giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh, because rejection is due to a defect in the narrator and acceptance is for modification, with jarh given precedence as will come, God willing, he intended to remove this claim and said: (And this is) not (from) the chapter (of giving precedence to ta'dil over jarh) as (he) claimed (in al-Badi'. Rather, acting upon his report is a tawthiq of him, for the action of a mujtahid is a tawthiq, and the leaving of action is not a jarh, because it is possible that it is due to finding a stronger or equal counter-evidence.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage (a ruling with reasoning) discusses three indicators (mu'arrafat) of a narrator's 'adala: (1) a judge's ruling based on his testimony, (2) a mujtahid's action on his narration, and (3) the silence of the Salaf about him when his narration is known. The Hanafi position is that if the Salaf were silent or differed, the narrator is considered known and his report can be acted upon; if only criticism appears, it is rejected; if nothing appears, it is not obligatory but permissible to act. The example of Fatima bint Qais is given: 'Umar rejected her hadith, but the Hanafis accept it as proof that silence does not imply rejection. The passage also addresses the objection that this might be a case of ta'dil over jarh, clarifying that acting on a report is tawthiq (declaring trustworthy), not ta'dil, and leaving action is not jarh due to possible counter-evidence. The text also discusses the status of Companions: only those of long companionship are automatically 'udul; others may be investigated.

Key Terms
معرفات العدالة (mu'arrafat al-'adala): Indicators that reveal a narrator's 'adala, such as a judge's ruling, a mujtahid's action, or the silence of the Salaf
سكوت السلف (sukut al-salaf): Silence of early scholars from criticizing a narrator whose hadith is known

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His hadith is rejected
B) His hadith can be acted upon in supererogatory matters
C) His hadith is obligatory to act upon
D) He is considered a liar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses contextual indicators like the silence of the Salaf to establish narrator integrity, and this is distinct from a simple preference of ta'dil over jarh.

Tadlis al-Taswiya and Its Ruling in Hanafi Usul
Defining tadlis al-taswiya and its ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tadlis al-taswiya, identify its condition, and apply the Hanafi ruling of tawaqquf to evaluate a mudallis's hadith.

Core Idea
Tadlis al-taswiya does not automatically reject a hadith; the correct Hanafi view is suspension until clarity.

In this passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut, the author discusses two types of tadlis (concealing defects in a chain of narration) and focuses on tadlis al-taswiya—dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones. The ruling hinges on whether the mudallis's act of narrating implies tazkiya (endorsement) of the dropped narrator, a point of disagreement between those who accept mursal reports and those who reject them. The Hanafi position settles on tawaqquf (suspension) until the true state of the dropped narrator is clarified.

Guided Path
1
Define tadlis and its two types
First, recall that tadlis is concealing a defect in the isnad. The passage mentions two types: tadlis by dropping a weak narrator (tadlis al-taswiya) and the general form. Focus on the former.
Tadlis al-taswiya specifically drops a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones, relying on the mudallis's own assessment.
2
Identify the condition for tadlis al-taswiya
Note the text: 'تدليس التسوية إنما يكون إذا كان من بعد المسقط معاصرا' – tadlis al-taswiya only occurs if the dropped narrator is contemporary to the mudallis. If not, it is not considered tadlis.
Contemporaneity is a key condition; otherwise the dropping is not deceptive.
3
Analyze the dispute regarding acceptance
Those who reject mursal (nufat al-marasil) consider tadlis al-taswiya harmful and reject the hadith. Those who accept mursal accept it, arguing the mudallis's narration is a tazkiya of the dropped narrator.
The Hanafis generally accept mursal under certain conditions, but here the correct view is tawaqquf.
4
State the correct Hanafi position: tawaqquf
The passage concludes: 'والصحيح التوقف في حديثه حتى يظهر حقيقة الحال' – the correct view is to withhold judgment until the true state of the narrator becomes clear.
This suspension applies until the condition of the dropped narrator is verified.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a hadith reported by a known mudallis, do not accept or reject it outright. Research the dropped narrator's reliability to determine the hadith's strength.
Tawaqquf is a precautionary principle in Hanafi usul to avoid either accepting weak narrators or discarding sound hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کدر لا ، إلا إذا علم حال الراوي الذي وقع فيه التدليس، وقيل: هذا مبني على أن رواية الثقة توثيق أم لا، وفي كون رواية المدلس توثيقاً تأمل ( وأما ) التدليس بإسقاط ضعيف) وهو قوي عنده (من بين ثقتين وبعبارة أخرى : إسقاط مختلف فيه اعتماداً على كونه ثقة (وهو) تدليس التسوية فيضر عند نفاة المراسيل ،حجيتها، وأما عند من يقبل المراسيل فيقبل، لأن جزمه بالرواية توثيق للمسقط، كما في المرسل، لكن قبول إرسال المدلس لا يخلو عن (والصحيح عدم سقوطه أي سقوط هذا المدلس (العدم) صريح (الكذب) بل غاية ما فعل الرواية عن المجهول ولا غائبة فيها (بل) الصحيح (التوقف) في حديثه حتى يظهر حقيقة الحال، ثم تدليس التسوية إنما يكون إذا كان من بعد المسقط معاصراً وإلا فلا تدليس فافهم
It is not, except if the condition of the narrator who committed tadlis is known, and it is said: this is based on whether the narration of a trustworthy person is a tazkiya or not, and there is consideration in whether the narration of a mudallis is a tazkiya. (As for) tadlis by dropping a weak narrator—who is strong in his view—from between two trustworthy ones, in other words: dropping a disputed narrator relying on his being trustworthy, that is tadlis al-taswiya. It is harmful according to those who reject mursal reports as evidence, but according to those who accept mursal reports, it is accepted, because his certainty in narrating is a tazkiya of the dropped one, as in the mursal. However, acceptance of the mursal of a mudallis is not free from (and the correct is that his [the mudallis] credence is not fallen) but the utmost he did was narrating from an unknown person, and there is no disparagement in it. Rather, the correct is to withhold regarding his hadith until the true state becomes clear. Then tadlis al-taswiya only occurs if the dropped person is contemporary, otherwise there is no tadlis, so understand.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage discusses two forms of tadlis and their rulings. The author clarifies that tadlis al-taswiya (dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones) is harmful only for those who reject mursal hadith. For those who accept mursal, it is accepted because the mudallis's act of narrating implies he considers the dropped narrator trustworthy. However, the correct view according to the Hanafi usul is tawaqquf (suspension) regarding the hadith of a mudallis until his condition is clarified. The passage also specifies that tadlis al-taswiya only applies when the dropped narrator is contemporary to the mudallis; otherwise it is not considered tadlis.

Key Terms
التدليس (al-tadlis): Concealing a defect in the chain of narration
تدليس التسوية (tadlis al-taswiya): Dropping a weak narrator between two trustworthy ones
المراسيل (al-marasil): Reports where a successor directly narrates from the Prophet without mentioning the companion

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Accepted absolutely
B) Rejected absolutely
C) Suspended until clarification
D) Accepted only if he is trustworthy

Key Takeaway
Tadlis al-taswiya leads to tawaqquf (suspension) until the status of the dropped narrator is clarified, a balanced Hanafi principle.

Three Methods to Establish a Narrator's Trustworthiness
Explanation of three identifiers of 'adala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi methods for establishing a narrator's 'adala and apply the criteria for the silence of the Salaf, distinguishing between accepted and rejected narrations.

Core Idea
A narrator's trustworthiness is established by a judge's ruling, a mujtahid's practice, or the Salaf's silence – but each has conditions.

In this passage from Musallam al-Thubut, the author outlines three ways to confirm a narrator's integrity ('adala): the ruling of a judge, the action of a mujtahid, and the silence of the early Muslims (Salaf) when a narration becomes widespread. These are essential tools for evaluating hadith and determining which narrations are acceptable. The third method, silence of the Salaf, is particularly contested and requires careful understanding of the Hanafi position, which accepts it as a form of implicit tazkiya.

Guided Path
1
List the three methods
Identify the three methods mentioned: (1) a judge's ruling based on the witness's testimony, (2) a mujtahid's acting upon a narration (implying he trusts the narrator), and (3) the silence of the Salaf when a narrator's reports become known.
2
Examine conditions for each method
For the judge's ruling and the mujtahid's action, both the judge and mujtahid must themselves be trustworthy, and the ruling must be based solely on the witness's testimony (no other basis). For silence of the Salaf, the narrator's reports must be widespread and the Salaf must have the ability to criticize but choose not to.
The text specifically conditions: 'not absolutely, but when both are trustworthy' for the first two methods.
3
Analyze the dispute on silence of the Salaf
Many hadith scholars reject silence as a valid form of tazkiya, while Hanafis accept it under specific conditions. Study the Hanafi position: the Salaf's silence indicates that the narrator is acceptable because they would not remain silent about a blameworthy person.
The example of Fatima bint Qais shows that even if some like 'Umar rejected her hadith, it was not due to her lack of 'adala but other reasons.
4
Understand the nuance about Companions
The author clarifies that the ruling of 'adala for Companions applies only to those with long companionship and known for jurisprudence or narration, not to those who merely met the Prophet briefly.
This prevents applying the silence method to all Companions indiscriminately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ومن المعرفات) للعدالة حكم الحاكم أي القاضي إذا حكم بشهادته (وعمل المجتهد) براويته، لكن لا مطلقاً، بل حال كونهما عدلين (شارطين للعدالة) وهذا إذا لم يكن له مستند آخر ولا يكون هو ثالث الشهداء (و) من المعرفات أيضاً (سكوت السلف) عن الطعن (عند اشتهار روايته إذ لا يسكتون) بعدالتهم على منكر) والعمل بخبر المطعون منكر، لكن هذا عند الاستطاعة فإن قبله بعض من السلف ورده بعض فكثير من أهل الحديث (على الرد والحنفية على القبول فإنهم قالوا الراوي إن كان غير معروف بالفقاهة ولا بالرواية بل إنما عرف بحديث أو حديثين فإن قبله الأئمة وسكتوا عنه عند ظهور الرواية أو اختلفوا كان كالمعروف وإن لم يظهر منهم غير الطعن كان مردوداً وإن لم يظهر شيء منهم لم يجب العمل، بل يجوز، أن قائلاً: فيعمل به في المندوبات والفضائل والتواريخ ومثلوا المطعون بفاطمة بنت قيس فإنها روت زوجها طلق فبت الطلاق، فلم يجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لها نفقة وسكنى وقال : اعتدي في بيت ابن أم مكتوم فإنه رجل أعمى فردها أمير المؤمنين عمر لا نترك كتاب ربنا وسنة نبينا بقول امرأة لا ندري أصدقت أم كذبت، حفظت أم نسيت، وأم المؤمنين عائشة الصديقة رضي الله تعالى عنها قائلة : ألا تتقي الله تعالى، إنما أمرها بالاعتداد في بيت ابن أم مكتوم لأنه لم يكن لزوجها بيت غير ما هو عورة ومعنى ما ذكرنا ثابت في صحيح مسلم»، فإن قلت يظهر من كلامهم أن الحكم عام في الراوي مطلقاً، صحابياً كان أو غيره كما تدل الأمثلة والصحابة كلهم عدول فلا وجه لرد رواية الغير المعروف من الصحابة، وإن تكلم عليه البعض قلت سيجيء أن حكم العدالة إنما هو في الصحابي الذي طالت صحبته وكون هذا المجهول منه محل بحث بل طويل الصحبة إما فقيه أو معروف بالرواية، نعم يرد على من سمى الصحابي لمن صحب ولو ساعة، مع أن الصحبة أيضاً محل بحث، ولا يلزم من المعاصرة أو الاجتماع في بلد الصحبة فافهم
(And from the identifiers) of trustworthiness: the ruling of the judge, i.e., the qadi when he rules on his testimony; (and the action of the mujtahid) by narrating from him, but not absolutely, rather when both are trustworthy (conditioning trustworthiness). This is if he has no other basis and he is not the third witness. (And) from the identifiers also (the silence of the Salaf) from criticism (when his narration is widespread, for they would not remain silent) due to their integrity about an objectionable matter. And acting upon the report of a criticized person is objectionable, but this is when it is possible. For if some of the Salaf accepted him and some rejected, then most of the hadith scholars are upon rejection, while the Hanafis are upon acceptance, for they said: The narrator is not known for jurisprudence nor for narration but is known by one or two hadiths, so if the imams accepted him and remained silent about him when the narration appeared, or they differed, he is like the known one. If nothing appears from them except criticism, he is rejected. And if nothing appears from them, then acting upon it is not obligatory, but permissible. (Thus) it is acted upon in supererogatory and virtuous deeds and histories. And they gave the example of a criticized one: Fatima bint Qais, for she narrated that her husband divorced her irrevocably, so the Messenger of God (peace be upon him and his family and companions) made no maintenance or lodging for her and said: 'Spend your waiting period in the house of Ibn Umm Maktum, for he is a blind man.' So the Commander of the Faithful, Umar, rejected it saying: 'We will not abandon the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman we do not know whether she is truthful or lying, mindful or forgetful.' And the Mother of the Faithful, Aisha al-Siddiqa, may God be pleased with her, said: 'Do you not fear God? He only ordered her to observe her waiting period in the house of Ibn Umm Maktum because her husband had no house other than that which was a private place.' And the meaning of what we mentioned is established in Sahih Muslim. If you say: It appears from their statement that the ruling is general for any narrator absolutely, whether he is a Companion or not, as the examples indicate, and all the Companions are trustworthy, so there is no reason to reject the narration of an unknown Companion, even if some discuss it. I say: It will come that the ruling of trustworthiness applies only to a Companion who had a long companionship, and this unknown one being from them is subject to investigation. Rather, a long-term companion is either a jurist or known for narration. Yes, it is a criticism of one who calls a Companion anyone who accompanied for even an hour, while companionship itself is also a subject of investigation. And contemporaneity or meeting in a city does not necessitate companionship, so understand.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage discusses three methods by which a narrator's trustworthiness ('adala) can be established: (1) the ruling of a qadi (judge) based on his testimony, (2) the action of a mujtahid in narrating from him (subject to conditions), and (3) the silence of the Salaf (early Muslims) regarding a narrator when his narrations become widespread. The author then elaborates on the third method, noting a dispute: many hadith scholars reject silence as a valid form of tazkiya, while the Hanafis accept it, especially when the narrator is not well-known but the early imams accepted him or remained silent. The example of Fatima bint Qais illustrates this: her hadith about no maintenance for a thrice-divorced woman was accepted by some but rejected by 'Umar and defended by 'Aisha. The passage concludes with a clarification that the ruling of 'adala for Companions applies only to those who had a long companionship and were known for jurisprudence or narration, not to every person who merely met the Prophet briefly.

Key Terms
العدالة (al-‘adāla): Moral probity and integrity required for accepting a narrator's testimony
سكوت السلف (sukūt al-salaf): The silence of the early Muslims about a narrator's reported narrations, taken as an indication of his reliability
حكم الحاكم (ḥukm al-ḥākim): A judge's ruling based on a witness's testimony establishes that witness's 'adala
عمل المجتهد (‘amal al-mujtahid): A mujtahid's act of acting upon a narration indicates he considers the narrator trustworthy

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, when does silence of the Salaf serve as a valid method to establish a narrator's trustworthiness?
A) Only when the narrator is a Companion
B) When the narrator's reports are widespread and no criticism appears
C) Only when the narrator is known for jurisprudence
D) Silence is never a valid method

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes three identifiers of narrator trustworthiness, with the silence of the Salaf being a valid but conditional method that distinguishes them from many hadith scholars.

Jarh and Ta'dil: How Many Witnesses?
Debating whether tazkiya is established by one or two witnesses, with arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of witnesses required for tazkiya in riwaya versus shahada and apply the proof that the condition cannot exceed the conditioned.

Core Idea
Tazkiya for riwaya requires one witness; for shahada, two — the condition cannot be stricter than the conditioned.

In hadith criticism, establishing a narrator's trustworthiness (tazkiya) is essential. But how many witnesses are needed? This question touches on the nature of testimony versus narration. The Hanafi school draws a clear distinction between riwaya (narrating hadith) and shahada (court testimony), leading to different requirements. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the proofs, and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
State the controversy: how many witnesses are needed for jarh and tazkiya? Note the Hanafi distinction: one in riwaya, two in public shahada (and also private according to Imam Muhammad).
The chosen (mukhtar) view is the majority position.
2
Examine the first Hanafi proof from zann
The statement of a trustworthy person gives preponderant assumption (zann) of truth. Acting on zann is obligatory, so a single testimony is accepted. The objection based on shahada is countered: shahada requires caution due to biases, but number is required by text (Quran 2:282), not by analogy.
The text also notes that number does not eliminate negligence entirely; strong zann can come from one person.
3
Understand the second proof: condition vs. conditioned
The condition (tazkiya) cannot be stricter than the conditioned (the narrator being validated). Since the narrator is one person, one witness suffices.
This is a powerful usul principle: the means should not be more burdensome than the end.
4
Contrast with opposing views
Al-Baqillani says one suffices in both riwaya and shahada. Others say two in both. Note the thamarah al-khilaf: practical differences in accepting hadith or court testimony.
The Hanafi view balances probability and caution.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The chosen (mukhtar) position: one witness in riwaya, two in shahada (public tazkiya). This is the operative ruling.
This is the position of the majority of Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: الجرح والتعديل يثبت بواحد أي بتزكية واحد عدل (في الرواية) (و) يثبت (باثنين في الشهادة في تزكية العلانية عندهما، وفي السر أيضاً عند الإمام محمد(عند الأكثر) من الأئمة (وهو المختار وقيل يثبت باثنين فيهما) وقيل يثبت بواحد فيهما، وعليه القاضي) أبو بكر الباقلاني لنا أوّلاً كما أقول : قول العدل مرجح) قطعاً (فيظن الصدق) في أخباره (والعمل بالظن (واجب) فيجب العمل بقوله فيقبل، فإن قيل : منقوض بالشهادة قال، (وأما الشهادة فأخلق بالاحتياط لكثرة البواعث هناك على المساهلة كالصداقة والعداوة، فشرط فيه العدد، وفيه أن العدد لا ينفي المساهلة أيضاً، بل غايته الظن القوي، والظن كان حاصلاً بالواحد أيضاً، وأيضاً فتزكية السر والعلانية متساويتان في وجوب الاحتياط، فالأولى أن الشهادة شرط فيها العدد بالنص وتزكية العلانية شهادة معنى لاختصاصه بمجلس القضاء كالشهادة وإيجابها على القاضي الحكم مثلها فأعطيت حكمها (و) لنا :(ثانياً : لا يزيد شرط على مشروطه
Issue: Al-jarh and al-ta'dil are established by one, i.e., by the tazkiya of one trustworthy person (in riwaya), (and) are established (by two in testimony in public tazkiya according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and in private also according to Imam Muhammad. According to the majority of imams, (and it is the chosen view). And it is said: established by two in both. And it is said: established by one in both, and upon this is al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. Our evidence first: as I say: the statement of a trustworthy person is preponderant (rajih) definitively, so truth is assumed in his reports, and acting upon assumption (zann) is obligatory, so acting upon his statement is obligatory, thus it is accepted. If it is said: this is contradicted by testimony (shahada), he said: As for testimony, it is more deserving of caution because of the many motives for negligence there, such as friendship and enmity, so number is required in it. There is in it that number does not negate negligence either, rather its utmost is strong assumption, and assumption can also be obtained by one. Also, private and public tazkiya are equal in the necessity of caution. So the better view is that number is required in shahada by text, and public tazkiya is a shahada in meaning because it is specific to the court like shahada and obligates the judge to rule like it, so it is given its ruling. (And) for us (secondly): The condition cannot exceed the conditioned (the one narrating).
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage addresses the question of how many witnesses are needed to establish jarh or ta'dil of a narrator. The chosen Hanafi position (mukhtar) is that one witness suffices in riwaya (narration) matters, while two witnesses are required in shahada (testimony) for public tazkiya, and also for private tazkiya according to Imam Muhammad. Some say two in both, and al-Baqillani says one in both. Two proofs are provided: First, the statement of a trustworthy person gives preponderant assumption (zann), and acting on assumption is obligatory. For shahada, caution is needed due to potential biases, so the Quranic requirement of two witnesses applies. Second, the condition (shart) cannot be stricter than the conditioned (mashrut); since the narrator himself is being validated, one witness should suffice.

Key Terms
جرح (jarḥ): Disparagement of a narrator's integrity or memory
تعديل (ta‘dīl): Validation of a narrator's trustworthiness
تزكية (tazkiya): The act of declaring a narrator trustworthy
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony in a legal setting
رواية (riwāya): Narration of hadith

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One
B) Two
C) Four
D) None

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between riwaya and shahada: one witness suffices in the former, two in the latter, because the condition cannot be stricter than the conditioned.
